###begin article-title 0
###xml 55 78 55 78 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila melanogaster</italic>
###xml 55 78 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">Drosophila melanogaster</span>
Genetic screening for modifiers of the DREF pathway in Drosophila melanogaster: identification and characterization of HP6 as a novel target of DREF
###end article-title 0
###begin p 1
Present addresses: Hiroyuki Ida, Environmental Research Laboratory of Public Health, Kankyo Eisei Yakuhin Co. Ltd., 3-6-2 Hikaridai, Seika-cho, Soraku-gun, Kyoto 619-0237, Japan
###end p 1
###begin p 2
Hideki Yoshida, Terrence Donnelly Centre for Cellular and Biomolecular Research, University of Toronto, 160 College St., Toronto, Ontario, M5S 3E1, Canada
###end p 2
###begin p 3
Katsuhito Ohno, Department of Molecular Biology and Biochemistry, Nelson Biology Laboratory, Rutgers University, 604 Allison Road, Piscataway, NJ 08854, USA
###end p 3
###begin p 4
###xml 0 16 0 16 <!--CREATIVE COMMONS-->
CREATIVE COMMONSThis is an Open Access article distributed under the terms of the Creative Commons Attribution Non-Commercial License () which permits unrestricted non-commercial use, distribution, and reproduction in any medium, provided the original work is properly cited.
###end p 4
###begin p 5
###xml 114 124 114 124 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 383 386 383 386 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HP6</italic>
###xml 388 394 388 394 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pigeon</italic>
###xml 396 400 396 400 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lace</italic>
###xml 402 425 402 425 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">X box binding protein 1</italic>
###xml 430 437 430 437 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">guftagu</italic>
###xml 546 549 546 549 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HP6</italic>
###xml 762 772 762 772 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 934 941 934 941 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
###xml 964 974 964 974 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 1099 1102 1099 1102 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HP6</italic>
The DNA replication-related element-binding factor (DREF) regulates cell proliferation-related gene expression in Drosophila. By genetic screening, taking advantage of the rough eye phenotype of transgenic flies that express DREF in the eye discs, we identified 24 genes that suppressed and 12 genes that enhanced the rough eye phenotype when heterozygous for mutations. Five genes, HP6, pigeon, lace, X box binding protein 1 and guftagu were found to carry replication-related element (DRE) sequences in their 5'-flanking regions. Of these, the HP6 gene carries two sequences that match seven out of eight nucleotides of DRE and two additional sequences that match six out of eight nucleotides of DRE in the 5'-flanking region. Band mobility shift assays using Drosophila Kc cell nuclear extracts demonstrated DREF binding to two of these sites and chromatin immunoprecipitation using anti-DREF antibodies confirmed that this occurs in vivo. Knockdown of DREF in Drosophila S2 cells decreased the HP6 mRNA level. The results, taken together, indicate that DREF directly regulates expression of the HP6 gene. HP6 mRNA was detected throughout development by RT-PCR with highest levels in adult males. In addition, immunostaining analyses revealed colocalization of HP6 and DREF in nuclei at the apical tips in the testes.
###end p 5
###begin title 6
INTRODUCTION
###end title 6
###begin p 7
###xml 70 80 70 80 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 187 191 187 191 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B1 B2 B3 B4 B5 B6 B7 B8 B9 B10">1&#8211;10</xref>
###xml 308 309 308 309 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B1">1</xref>
###xml 310 312 310 312 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B11">11</xref>
###xml 313 315 313 315 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B12">12</xref>
###xml 527 528 527 528 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B1">1</xref>
###xml 631 633 631 633 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B13">13</xref>
###xml 806 808 806 808 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B14">14</xref>
###xml 809 811 809 811 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B15">15</xref>
Promoters of many DNA replication- and proliferation-related genes in Drosophila contain a common 8 bp palindromic sequence, 5'-TATCGATA, named the DNA replication-related element (DRE) (1-10). The requirement of DRE for promoter activity has been confirmed in both cultured cell and transgenic fly systems (1,11,12) and a specific DNA replication-related element-binding factor (DREF) has been identified. Molecular cloning of its cDNA has led to confirmation that DREF is a transcriptional activator of DRE-containing genes (1). It is also reported that DREF is a component of a transcription initiation complex containing TRF2 (13). In addition, the chromatin remodelling factor dMi-2 and a homeodomain protein Distal-less can bind to the DNA-binding domain of DREF to inhibit its DNA-binding activity (14,15).
###end p 7
###begin p 8
###xml 16 26 16 26 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 144 146 144 146 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B16">16</xref>
###xml 147 149 147 149 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B17">17</xref>
###xml 344 346 344 346 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B14">14</xref>
###xml 577 579 577 579 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B18">18</xref>
###xml 663 670 663 670 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
Searches of the Drosophila genome database have revealed the presence of 277 genes containing DRE-like sequences within their promoter regions (16,17) and immunostaining of polytene chromosomes of salivary glands with anti-DREF monoclonal antibodies demonstrated binding of DREF to a hundred discrete interband regions of polytene chromosomes (14). In addition, serial analysis of gene expression (SAGE) showed that many genes selectively expressed in dividing cells located anterior to the morphogenetic furrow of the eye imaginal disc carry DRE in their 5'-flanking regions (18). DREF may therefore regulate the expression of many genes and play multiple roles in vivo.
###end p 8
###begin p 9
###xml 233 235 233 235 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B19">19</xref>
###xml 469 471 469 471 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B20">20</xref>
###xml 620 622 620 622 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B21">21</xref>
###xml 623 625 623 625 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B22">22</xref>
Ectopic expression of the dominant-negative form of DREF using the GAL4-UAS targeted expression system causes inhibition of both endo-replication in larval salivary gland cells and mitotic DNA replication in eye imaginal disc cells (19). Ectopic expression of full length DREF in eye imaginal discs causes ectopic DNA synthesis and apoptosis in otherwise post-mitotic cells, and inhibits photoreceptor cell differentiation that results in a severe rough eye phenotype (20). RNAi mediated knockdown of DREF in growing tissues has also provided direct evidence that it is necessary for cell cycle and cell growth control (21,22).
###end p 9
###begin p 10
###xml 237 241 237 241 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dE2F</italic>
###xml 243 249 243 249 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">brahma</italic>
###xml 251 256 251 256 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">moira</italic>
###xml 261 264 261 264 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">osa</italic>
###xml 293 304 293 304 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Distal-less</italic>
###xml 366 368 366 368 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B20">20</xref>
###xml 540 542 540 542 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B23">23</xref>
###xml 627 633 627 633 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">brahma</italic>
###xml 635 640 635 640 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">moira</italic>
###xml 645 648 645 648 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">osa</italic>
###xml 721 723 721 723 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B20">20</xref>
###xml 896 898 896 898 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B24">24</xref>
###xml 1065 1068 1065 1068 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HP6</italic>
###xml 1070 1077 1070 1077 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">CG15636</italic>
###xml 1192 1195 1192 1195 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HP6</italic>
In order to identify novel targets of DREF, we have carried out a screening, taking advantage of the rough eye phenotype of the transgenic flies that express full length DREF in the eye imaginal discs. Our previous screen identified the dE2F, brahma, moira and osa gene as suppressors and the Distal-less gene as an enhancer of the DREF-induced rough eye phenotype (20). E2F is a transcription factor regulating the genes involved in cell cycle, while Brahma, Moira and Osa are components of the chromatin-remodelling Brahma (BRM) complex (23). Suppression of the DREF-induced rough eye phenotype by reduction of dosage of the brahma, moira, or osa suggests that the genes coding for the BRM complex are targets of DREF (20). These observations combined with molecular and biochemical analyses indicate that DREF is involved in transcriptional regulation of the genes coding for the BRM complex (24). In this study, we further identified 24 suppressors and 12 enhancers of the DREF-induced rough eye phenotype. One of the strongest suppressors was a mutant for the HP6 (CG15636) gene, which carries multiple DRE-like sequences in its 5'-flanking region. The present results indicate that the HP6 gene is one of the targets of the DRE/DREF regulatory system with major physiological significance.
###end p 10
###begin title 11
MATERIALS AND METHODS
###end title 11
###begin title 12
Fly stocks
###end title 12
###begin p 13
###xml 117 120 105 108 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">vlR</sup>
###xml 108 124 102 112 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dp&#176;<sup>vlR</sup>/SM5</italic>
###xml 131 132 119 120 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D</sup>
###xml 129 136 117 124 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dp<sup>D</sup>/SM1</italic>
###xml 191 201 179 189 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 291 293 279 281 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B19">19</xref>
###xml 383 385 371 373 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B25">25</xref>
Fly stocks were maintained at 25degreesC on standard food. The Canton S fly was used as a wild type strain. dpdegreesvlR/SM5 and dpD/SM1 were obtained from the Kyoto Institute of Technology, Drosophila Genetic Resource Center (Japan). The UAS-DREF transgenic fly line was described earlier (19) as was the transgenic fly line (line number 16) carrying pGMR-GAL4 on the X chromosome (25). All other stocks used in this study were obtained from the Bloomington, Indiana, stock centre.
###end p 13
###begin title 14
Establishment of transgenic flies
###end title 14
###begin p 15
###xml 82 84 82 84 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B26">26</xref>
###xml 159 161 159 161 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B27">27</xref>
###xml 216 219 216 219 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HP6</italic>
###xml 249 252 249 252 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HP6</italic>
P-element-mediated germ line transformation was carried out as described earlier (26). F1 transformants were selected on the basis of white-eye colour rescue (27). Two independent lines were established for the pUAS-HP6. We used line 2 carrying UAS-HP6 on the third chromosome in the present study.
###end p 15

###xml 197 199 197 199 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B11">11</xref>
###xml 373 376 373 376 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HP6</italic>

The DRE-PM oligonucleotide is a two-base substitution derivative of DRE-P (11). For band mobility shift assays, the following oligonucleotides were synthesized. ###begin title 85
Plasmid construction
###end title 85
###begin p 86
###xml 59 69 59 69 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 176 179 176 179 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bgl</italic>
###xml 186 189 186 189 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kpn</italic>
###xml 216 219 216 219 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bgl</italic>
###xml 226 229 226 229 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Kpn</italic>
###xml 258 260 258 260 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B28">28</xref>
To construct the pUAS-HP6 plasmid, PCR was performed using Drosophila genomic DNA as a template and primers 5'Bgl2P and 3'Kpn1P in combination. PCR products were digested with BglII and KpnI and inserted between the BglII and KpnI sites ofthe pUAST plasmid (28).
###end p 86
###begin p 87
###xml 78 94 78 94 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Escherichia coli</italic>
###xml 224 227 224 227 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bam</italic>
###xml 234 237 234 237 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Xho</italic>
###xml 264 267 264 267 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bam</italic>
###xml 274 277 274 277 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Xho</italic>
###xml 78 94 <span type="species:ncbi:562">Escherichia coli</span>
To construct the pGST-HP6 plasmid for expression of GST-HP6 fusion protein in Escherichia coli, PCR was performed using pUAS-HP6 as a template and primers 5'BamH1P and 3'Xho1P in combination. PCR products were digested with BamHI and XhoI and inserted between the BamHI and XhoI sites of pGex6p-1 (GE healthcare).
###end p 87
###begin title 88
Expression of GST fusion proteins and purification of HP6 protein
###end title 88
###begin p 89
###xml 41 48 41 48 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">E. coli</italic>
###xml 94 96 94 96 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B29">29</xref>
###xml 264 265 263 264 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">g</italic>
###xml 642 644 629 631 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B30">30</xref>
###xml 41 53 <span type="species:ncbi:511693">E. coli BL21</span>
Expression of GST-HP6 fusion proteins in E. coli BL21 was carried out as described elsewhere (29). Lysates of cells were prepared by sonication in PBS containing 1 mM PMSF, and 1 muM each of pepstatin and leupeptin. Lysates were cleared by centrifugation at 12 000g for 20 min at 4degreesC and applied to glutathione-Sepharose (GE healthcare). The columns were washed with PBS containing 0.5 M NaCl and 0.1% Triton X-100, then with a buffer containing 150 mM NaCl, 50 mM Tris-HCl pH 7.2, 1 mM EDTA and 1 mM dithiothreitol (DTT). The included GST-HP6 fusion proteins were treated with Precision protease (GE healthcare) for 16 h at 4degreesC (30) and then eluted with PBS.
###end p 89
###begin title 90
Antibodies
###end title 90
###begin p 91
###xml 405 406 405 406 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B1">1</xref>
###xml 407 409 407 409 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B31">31</xref>
###xml 79 85 <span type="species:ncbi:9986">rabbit</span>
The purified HP6 protein were used to elicit polyclonal antibody production in rabbit. Polyclonal antibodies reacting with HP6 were affinity-purified from anti-serum using the N-hydroxysuccinimide (NHS)-activated Sepharose HP (GE healthcare) coupled with GST-HP6 fusion protein after passage through GST-conjugated Sepharose HP. Preparation of anti-DREF monoclonal antibodies was as described previously (1,31).
###end p 91
###begin title 92
Western immunoblot analysis
###end title 92
###begin p 93
###xml 15 23 15 23 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Canton S</italic>
###xml 45 50 45 50 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Act5C</italic>
###xml 91 103 91 103 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">UAS-Flag-HP6</italic>
###xml 108 113 108 113 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Act5C</italic>
###xml 328 329 325 326 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">g</italic>
###xml 1037 1048 <span type="species:ncbi:3704">horseradish</span>
###xml 1074 1079 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
###xml 1093 1099 <span type="species:ncbi:9986">rabbit</span>
Adult males of Canton S, a line carrying the Act5C-GAL4 transgene and a line carrying both UAS-Flag-HP6 and Act5C-GAL4 transgenes were frozen in liquid nitrogen and homogenized in a solution containing 50 mM Tris-borate (pH 6.8), 2% SDS, 6% beta-ME, 10% glycerol and 0.1% bromophenol blue. Homogenates were centrifuged at 17 800g at 4degreesC for 5 min, and extracts (100 mug of protein) were electrophoretically separated on SDS-15% polyacrylamide gels and transferred to polyvinylidene difluoride (PVDF) membranes (Bio-Rad) in a solution containing 25 mM Tris, 190 mM glycine and 20% methanol for 1 h at 25degreesC. Blotted membranes were blocked with Tris-buffered saline (TBS) solution (20 mM Tris-HCl, pH 7.4 and 150 mM NaCl) containing 0.05% Tween 20 and 5% skim milk for 1 h at 25degreesC and then incubated with an anti-HP6 polyclonal antibody at a 1 : 500 dilution, or the anti-FLAGM5 antibody (Sigma) at a 1 : 2000 dilution at 4degreesC for 16 h. After washing with TBS containing 0.05% Tween 20, the blots were incubated with horseradish peroxidase-labelled anti-mouse IgG and anti-rabbit IgG (GE healthcare) at a 1 : 20 000 dilution for 1 h at 25degreesC. Detection was performed with ECL Western blotting detection reagents (GE healthcare).
###end p 93
###begin title 94
Scanning electron microscopy
###end title 94
###begin p 95
Adult flies were anesthetized, mounted on stages and observed under a Hitachi S-3000 scanning electron microscope in the low vacuum mode.
###end p 95
###begin title 96
Band mobility shift assays
###end title 96
###begin p 97
###xml 67 68 67 68 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B4">4</xref>
###xml 160 161 160 161 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B4">4</xref>
###xml 373 375 373 375 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">32</sup>
Band mobility shift analysis was performed as reported previously (4), with minor modifications. Kc cell nuclear extracts were prepared as described elsewhere (4) and incubated in a reaction mixture containing 15 mM Hepes, pH 7.6, 60 mM KCl, 0.1 mM EDTA, 1 mM DTT, 12% glycerol, 0.05 mg/ml poly(dI-dC), 0.05 mg/ml Salmon sperm DNA (average size 0.2 kb) and double-stranded 32P-labelled synthetic oligonucleotides (10 000 cpm) for 15 min at 0degreesC. When necessary, unlabelled oligonucleotides were added as competitors at this step. DNA-protein complexes were electrophoretically resolved on 4% polyacrylamide gels in 50 mM Tris-borate, pH 8.3, 1 mM EDTA and 2.5% glycerol at 25degreesC. Gels were dried and autoradiographed.
###end p 97
###begin p 98
###xml 132 133 132 133 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B1">1</xref>
###xml 294 296 294 296 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">32</sup>
Band mobility shift assays were also performed in the presence of anti-DREF monoclonal antibody 1, anti-DREF monoclonal antibody 4 (1) or anti-GST monoclonal antibody 1 as a control. Kc cell nuclear extracts were mixed with each antibody, incubated for 2 h on ice, added to mixtures containing 32P-labelled synthetic oligonucleotides (10 000 cpm) and 0.05 mg/ml poly(dI-dC), 0.05 mg/ml Salmon sperm DNA (average size 0.2 kb) and then incubated for 15 min at 0degreesC as described above.
###end p 98
###begin title 99
Immunostaining of polytene chromosomes
###end title 99
###begin p 100
###xml 76 82 76 82 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">et al.</italic>
###xml 138 140 138 140 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B32">32</xref>
###xml 178 184 <span type="species:ncbi:9913">bovine</span>
###xml 437 442 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
Polytene chromosome spreads were prepared according to the protocol of Zink et al. from Canton S wild-type wandering third instar larvae (32) and stored in PBS-0.05% Tween 20-1% bovine serum albumin (BSA) at 4degreesC for 16 h before incubation with anti-DREF monoclonal antibody at a 1 : 1000 dilution at 4degreesC for 16 h. After extensive washing with PBS-0.05% Tween 20-1% BSA, samples were incubated at 25degreesC for 1 h with anti-mouse IgG conjugated with Alexa 594 (Invitrogen) at a 1 : 400 dilution. The chromosomes were then washed with PBS-0.05% Tween 20-1% BSA and mounted in Fluoroguard Antifade Reagent (Bio-Rad) for microscopic observation.
###end p 100
###begin title 101
Immunostaining of testes
###end title 101
###begin p 102
###xml 86 88 86 88 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B33">33</xref>
###xml 137 141 <span type="species:ncbi:9925">goat</span>
###xml 413 419 <span type="species:ncbi:9986">rabbit</span>
###xml 471 476 <span type="species:ncbi:10090">mouse</span>
Preparation of testes from 1-day-old adult males for immunostaining was as described (33). After blocking with PBS containing 10% normal goat serum, the preparations were incubated with anti-DREF monoclonal antibody at a 1 : 1000 dilution or with an anti-HP6 polyclonal antibody at a 1 : 500 dilution at 4degreesC for 16 h. After extensive washing with PBS, samples were incubated at 25degreesC for 2 h with anti-rabbit IgG conjugated with Alexa 594 (Invitrogen) or anti-mouse IgG conjugated with Alexa 488 (Invitrogen) at a 1 : 400 dilution. The samples were mounted in Fluoroguard Antifade Reagent (Bio-Rad) for microscopic observation.
###end p 102
###begin title 103
Chromatin immunoprecipitation
###end title 103
###begin p 104
###xml 132 133 132 133 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">7</sup>
###xml 511 512 497 498 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">g</italic>
###xml 1062 1063 1022 1023 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">3</sub>
###xml 791 797 <span type="species:ncbi:9986">rabbit</span>
We performed chromatin immunoprecipitation using a Chip Assay kit as recommended by the manufacturer (Upstate). Approximately 1 x 107 S2 cells were fixed in 1% formaldehyde at 37degreesC for 10 min and then quenched in 125 mM glycine for 5 min at 25degreesC. Cells were washed twice in PBS containing protease inhibitors (1 mM PMSF, 1 mug/ml aprotinin and 1 mug/ml pepstatin A) and lysed in 2 ml of SDS lysis buffer. Lysates were sonicated to break DNA into fragments of less than 1 kb and centrifuged at 15 300g for 10 min at 4degreesC. The sonicated cell supernatants were diluted 10-fold in Chip Dilution Buffer and pre-cleared with 80 mul Salmon Sperm DNA/Protein A agarose-50% slurry for 30 min at 4degreesC. After brief centrifugation, each supernatant was incubated with 1 mug of the rabbit IgG or anti-DREF polyclonal antibody for 16 h at 4degreesC. Salmon Sperm DNA/Protein A agarose-50% slurry was added, followed by incubation for 1 h at 4degreesC. After washing, immunoprecipitated DNA was eluted with elution buffer containing 1% SDS and 0.1 M NaHCO3. Then the protein-DNA crosslinks were reversed by heating at 65degreesC for 4 h. After deproteinization with proteinase K, DNA was recovered by phenol-chloroform extraction and ethanol precipitation.
###end p 104
###begin p 105
###xml 159 161 159 161 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B34">34</xref>
Immunoprecipitated DNA fragments were detected by quantitative real time PCR using SYBR Green I (Takara) and the Applied Biosystems 7500 Real Time PCR system (34). The DeltaDeltaCT value for each sample was calculated by subtracting the CT value for the input sample from the CT value obtained for the immunoprecipitated samples. Fold differences relative to the controls using non-immune IgG were then calculated by raising 2 to the DeltaDeltaCT power. The DeltaDeltaCT was calculated by subtracting the DeltaCT value for that for the sample immunoprecipitated with control IgG.
###end p 105
###begin title 106
Quantitative RT-PCR
###end title 106
###begin p 107
###xml 6 7 6 7 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">6</sup>
###xml 736 737 733 734 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">T</sub>
###xml 758 760 755 757 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B35">35</xref>
###xml 767 779 764 773 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">&#946;-tubulin</italic>
1 x 106 S2 cells were plated in 6-well dishes in 2 ml M3 medium containing 30 mug/well of DREF double stranded RNAs (DREFdsRNA) or LacZdsRNA for 1 h. After the incubation, 3 ml of 10% FBS-M3 medium was added to each well. At 5 days after the dsRNA treatment, total RNA was isolated from cells using TrizolReagent (Invitrogen) and 1 mug aliquots were reverse transcribed with oligo dT primer using a Takara high fidelity RNA PCR kit (Takara). Then, real time PCR was performed with a SYBR Green I kit (Takara) and the Applied Biosystems 7500 Real Time PCR system using one mul of reverse transcribed sample per reaction. Levels of mRNAs in the DREFdsRNA or LacZdsRNA treated cells and in no dsRNA treated cells were investigated by the CT comparative method (35). The beta-tubulin gene was chosen as a negative control. Rp49 was used as an endogenous reference gene. Experiments were performed in triplicate for each of three RNA batches isolated separately.
###end p 107
###begin title 108
Developmental RT-PCR
###end title 108
###begin p 109
###xml 16 26 16 26 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 273 276 273 276 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Bca</italic>
###xml 347 350 347 350 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HP6</italic>
###xml 355 359 355 359 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RP49</italic>
###xml 392 400 392 400 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Pyrobest</italic>
###xml 400 402 400 402 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">TM</sup>
###xml 490 493 490 493 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HP6</italic>
###xml 522 526 522 526 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">RP49</italic>
Total RNAs from Drosophila bodies at various developmental stages were purified with TRIZOL (Invitrogen). For RT-PCR, mRNAs were purified using an Oligotex-dT30 <Super> mRNA Purification kit (Takara Bio) and then were used for cDNA synthesis using an oligo d(T) primer and Bca PLUS RTase (Takara Bio) according to the manufacturer's instructions. HP6 and RP49 DNA were amplified by PCR using PyrobestTM DNA Polymerase (Takara Bio) with primer oligonucleotides CG15636P and CG15636antiP for HP6 and RP49P and RP49antiP for RP49. The PCR conditions included one cycle of 2 min at 94degreesC followed by 25 cycles of 94degreesC for 30 s, 52degreesC or 55degreesC for 30 s and 72degreesC for 1 min. All the PCR reactions were performed within the range of linear amplification and PCR products were separated on 2% agarose gels.
###end p 109
###begin title 110
RESULTS
###end title 110
###begin title 111
###xml 96 99 96 99 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HP6</italic>
Genetic screening of modifiers of the DREF-induced rough eye phenotype and identification of an HP6 mutation as a dominant suppressor
###end title 111
###begin p 112
###xml 73 81 73 81 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">GMR-GAL4</italic>
###xml 151 156 151 156 <sub xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">1-709</sub>
###xml 143 156 143 156 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">UAS-DREF<sub>1-709</sub></italic>
###xml 159 161 159 161 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B19">19</xref>
###xml 162 164 162 164 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B28">28</xref>
###xml 367 369 367 369 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B36">36</xref>
###xml 436 438 436 438 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B20">20</xref>

colspan="1">Suppression</td></tr></tbody></table><table-wrap-foot><fn><p textid="114">Bold characters indicate deficiency lines used in the previous study (20)</p></fn></table-wrap-foot></table-wrap>
As reported previously, we have established transgenic fly lines bearing GMR-GAL4 and DREF cDNAs under the control of a GAL4-binding sequence (UAS-DREF1-709) (19,28). Over-expression of DREF induced ectopic DNA synthesis and apoptosis, and inhibited the photoreceptor cell differentiation in eye imaginal discs and adult flies exhibited a severe rough eye phenotype (36). Since the eye phenotype does not impair viability or fertility (20), these flies serve as a genetic tool to screen for modifying mutations. Previous studies identified 5 and 17 deletion regions that modify the DREF-induced rough eyes phenotype in the X and the second chromosome, respectively (20). In order to identify genes in these genomic regions that are responsible for modification of the DREF-induced rough eye phenotype, various mutants mapped in and around the 22 genomic regions (5D1-2; 5E, 7D1; 7D5-6, 9B1-2; 10A1-2, 11A2; 11B9, 19A5; 19D3, 21A1; 21B7-8, 21B8-C1; 21C8-D1, 21D2-3; 21F2-22A1, 25D2-4; 26B2-5, 32F1-3; 33F1-2, 35D1; 35D4, 35D2; 35F1-2, 35D2-4; 35E2-6, 36A8-9; 36E1-2, 36E4-36F1; 38A6-7, 37B2-12; 38D2-5, 37C2-5; 38B2-C1, 37D1-2; 38C1-2, 41A, 48A-B, 55A-55F, 57B4; 58B) were collected and used to cross with transgenic flies expressing DREF (Table 1). DRE and DRE-like sequences are located at positions &#8211;1013 to &#8211;1006 (DRE 2), &#8211;161 to &#8211;154 (DRE 1&#945;), &#8211;139 to &#8211;132 (DRE 1&#946;) and &#8211;123 to &#8211;116 (DRE1&#947;). DRE1 comprises DRE 1&#945;, DRE 1&#946; and DRE 1&#947;. Nucleotides that do not match to DRE consensus sequences are shown in small letters. A P-element is inserted 43 bp upstream of the termination codon of the <italic>HP6</italic> gene. The regions (DRE1 and DRE2) used as probes for band mobility shift assays are indicated.</p></caption><graphic xlink:href="gkn1068f2"/></fig>
Out of 238 independent mutant lines examined, 27 lines suppressed, while 19 lines enhanced the rough eye phenotype when they were heterozygous for the mutations (Figure 1D to F, Table 1). Under the scanning electron microscope, eyes of these heterozygous mutant flies appeared normal (data not shown). The other mutant lines apparently exerted no detectable effects on the DREF-induced rough eye phenotype. Cytological locations of these negative lines are listed in . Data base search revealed that 24 genes are responsible for the suppression and 12 genes for the enhancement. One of the strongest levels of suppression of the rough eye phenotype was observed with the P-element insertion line P{w + mGT = GT1}CG15636 (Figure 1B). The suppression could be reverted under dysgenic conditions (Figure 1C), suggesting the mutation induced by the P-element insertion to be truly responsible for the suppression. The Berkeley Drosophila genome project database () revealed that the P-element is inserted 43 bp upstream of the termination codon of the HP6 (CG15636) gene (Figure 2) and Greil et al. (37) reported that the mutant is semi-lethal. In contrast coexpression of HP6 further enhanced the DREF-induced rough eye phenotype in compared with the control flies coexpressing LacZ (Figure 1G and H), despite that overexpression of HP6 alone in the eye imaginal disc exerted only a marginal effect on the adult eye morphology (Figure 1I). (D) GMR-GAL4/+; UAS-DREF/rps26; +/+. (E) GMR-GAL4/+; UAS-DREF/pepck; +/+. (F) GMR-GAL4/+; UAS-DREF/star; +/+. (G) GMR-GAL4/+; UAS-DREF/+; UAS-nlslacZ/+. (H) GMR-GAL4/UAS-HP6; UAS-DREF/+; +/+. (I) GMR-GAL4/UAS-HP6; +/+; +/+. Bar indicates 50 mum.Figure 2.DRE and DRE-like sequences in the 5'-flanking regions of the HP6 gene. The translation initiation site is numbered as +1. DRE and DRE-like sequences are located at positions -1013 to -1006 (DRE 2), -161 to -154 (DRE 1alpha), -139 to -132 (DRE 1beta) and -123 to -116 (DRE1gamma). ###begin p 118
###xml 68 71 68 71 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HP6</italic>
###xml 286 294 286 294 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 473 481 462 470 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F2">Figure 2</xref>
###xml 623 624 612 613 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B4">4</xref>
###xml 709 711 698 700 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B11">11</xref>
###xml 712 714 701 703 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B38">38</xref>
###xml 767 770 756 759 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HP6</italic>
###xml 815 818 804 807 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HP6</italic>
We searched for DRE like sequences in the 5'-flanking region of the HP6 gene from the NCBI database, and found two sequences that match seven out of the eight nucleotides of DRE and two additional sequences that match six out of the eight nucleotides within the 1.4 kb upstream region (Figure 2). We named these sites as DRE1alpha (-161 to -154), DRE1beta (-139 to -132), DRE1gamma (-123 to -116) and DRE2 (-1013 to -1006) with respect to the translation initiation codon (Figure 2). It is reported that stimulatory effects of DRE can be observed at positions within at least 2.5 kb from the transcription initiation site (4) and sequences matching six out of eight nucleotides of DRE have promoter activity (11,38). Therefore, all of these DRE-like sequences of the HP6 gene likely play roles in regulation of the HP6 gene promoter activity.
###end p 118
###begin title 119
###xml 52 55 52 55 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HP6</italic>
DREF binds to the chromosomal region containing the HP6 gene
###end title 119
###begin p 120
###xml 73 76 73 76 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HP6</italic>
###xml 308 310 308 310 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B14">14</xref>
###xml 379 382 379 382 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HP6</italic>
###xml 439 449 439 449 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 504 507 504 507 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HP6</italic>
###xml 512 517 512 517 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dumpy</italic>
###xml 557 560 557 560 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HP6</italic>
###xml 589 593 589 593 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dump</italic>
###xml 596 598 596 598 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dp</italic>
###xml 629 652 629 652 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">P{w + mGT = GT1}CG15636</italic>
###xml 673 676 673 676 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HP6</italic>
###xml 686 688 686 688 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dp</italic>
###xml 806 808 806 808 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dp</italic>
###xml 834 837 828 831 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">vlR</sup>
###xml 825 841 825 835 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dp&#176;<sup>vlR</sup>/SM5</italic>
###xml 848 849 842 843 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">D</sup>
###xml 846 854 840 848 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dp<sup>D</sup>/SM1.</italic>
###xml 916 918 910 912 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dp</italic>
###xml 1029 1031 1023 1025 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dp</italic>
###xml 1137 1140 1131 1134 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HP6</italic>
To examine whether DREF locates to the chromosomal region containing the HP6 gene, we carried out immunostaining of salivary gland polytene chromosomes in third instar larvae with anti-DREF monoclonal antibodies. DREF signals are detected in a number of discrete regions throughout the polytene chromosomes (14). Careful inspection allowed the mapping of signals for DREF at the HP6 gene locus, 25A1, on the 2L chromosome (). The Berkeley Drosophila genome project database revealed that only two genes (HP6 and dumpy) are located in this 25A1 locus. Since HP6 is located in the intron of dumpy (dp), P-element insertion in line P{w + mGT = GT1}CG15636 may affect not only HP6 but also dp gene expression. We therefore crossed DREF-overexpressing flies with two independent X ray-induced homozygous lethal dp mutant strains, dpdegreesvlR/SM5 and dpD/SM1. However no effect on the DREF-induced rough eye phenotype by dp mutation was observed (). Furthermore there is no DRE like sequence within the 2 kb 5'-flanking region of the dp gene. It is therefore very likely that DREF binds to DRE-like sequences in the 5'-flanking region of the HP6 gene in the salivary glands.
###end p 120

To examine this directly, oligonucleotide DRE1 containing the region from DRE1alpha (-161 to -154) to DRE1gamma (-123 to -116), oligonucleotide DRE1gamma containing the DRE1gamma (-123 to -116) region and oligonucleotide DRE2 containing the DRE2 (-1013 to -1006) region (Figure 2) were chemically synthesized and used for band mobility shift assays. As previously noted (4), specific DNA protein complexes could be detected with Kc cell nuclear extracts and the oligonucleotide DRE-P carrying the DRE sequence in the PCNA gene (Figure 3A). The shifted bands were effectively diminished by adding unlabelled oligonucleotides DRE1 and DRE2. Although DRE1 carrying mutations in either DRE1alpha or DRE1beta also effectively competed against DRE-P, oligonucleotide DRE1 carrying mutations in DRE1gamma less effectively competed. These results suggest that DREF has affinity for the region containing DRE1gamma and DRE2. The amounts of competitors were 100- or 400-fold molar ratios. Anti-GST Mab1, anti-GST monoclonal antibody 1; anti-DREFMab1, anti-DREF monoclonal antibody 1; anti-DREFMab4, anti-DREF monoclonal antibody 4; DRE-P, oligonucleotide containing the DRE sequence of the Drosophila PCNA gene; DRE-PM, DRE-P having a mutation in the DRE sequence; DRE2, oligonucleotide containing the DRE2 sequence of the HP6 gene; DRE2M, DRE2 having mutations in the DRE-like sequence; DRE1, oligonucleotide containing the DRE1 sequence of the HP6 gene; DRE1M, DRE1 having mutations in the DRE1alphabetagamma sequences; DRE1alphaM, DRE1 having mutations in the DRE1alpha sequence; DRE1betaM, DRE1 having mutations in DRE1betasequence; DRE1gammaM, DRE1 having mutations in the DRE1gamma sequence.

###begin p 123
###xml 37 41 37 41 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">PCNA</italic>
###xml 86 88 86 88 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">32</sup>
###xml 139 140 139 140 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">A</bold>
###xml 149 150 149 150 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">B</bold>
###xml 167 168 163 164 <bold xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">C</bold>
###xml 576 591 572 587 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila PCNA</italic>
###xml 709 712 705 708 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HP6</italic>
###xml 832 835 828 831 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HP6</italic>
Complex formation between DRE in the PCNA gene promoter and Kc cell nuclear extracts. 32P-labelled double stranded oligonucleotides DRE-P (A), DRE2 (B) and DRE1gamma (C) were incubated with Kc cell nuclear extracts in the presence of the indicated competitor oligonucleotides or anti-DREF monoclonal antibodies. The amounts of competitors were 100- or 400-fold molar ratios. Anti-GST Mab1, anti-GST monoclonal antibody 1; anti-DREFMab1, anti-DREF monoclonal antibody 1; anti-DREFMab4, anti-DREF monoclonal antibody 4; DRE-P, oligonucleotide containing the DRE sequence of the Drosophila PCNA gene; DRE-PM, DRE-P having a mutation in the DRE sequence; DRE2, oligonucleotide containing the DRE2 sequence of the HP6 gene; DRE2M, DRE2 having mutations in the DRE-like sequence; DRE1, oligonucleotide containing the DRE1 sequence of the HP6 gene; DRE1M, DRE1 having mutations in the DRE1alphabetagamma sequences; DRE1alphaM, DRE1 having mutations in the DRE1alpha sequence; DRE1betaM, DRE1 having mutations in DRE1betasequence; DRE1gammaM, DRE1 having mutations in the DRE1gamma sequence.
###end p 123
###begin p 124
###xml 132 141 128 137 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">Figures 3</xref>
###xml 290 299 282 291 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">Figures 3</xref>
###xml 415 424 407 416 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">Figures 3</xref>
###xml 658 667 650 659 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F3">Figures 3</xref>
###xml 791 794 779 782 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HP6</italic>
###xml 809 817 797 805 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vitro</italic>
When the oligonucleotides DRE2 or DRE1gamma were mixed with Kc cell nuclear extracts, specific DNA-protein complexes were detected [Figures 3B (lane 1) and 3C (lane 1)], which were diminished by addition of an excess amount of unlabelled DRE2 and DRE1gamma oligonucleotides as competitors [Figures 3B (lanes 2 and 3) and 3C (lanes 2 and 3)] but not of oligonucleotides carrying mutations in the DRE-like sequences [Figures 3B (lanes 4 and 5) and 3C (lanes 4 and 5)]. Furthermore, the specific DNA-protein complexes were either diminished or super shifted by adding anti-DREF monoclonal antibodies, but not by adding the control anti-GST monoclonal antibody [Figures 3B (lanes 7 and 8) and 3C (lanes 7 and 8)]. These results indicate that DREF can bind to DRE1gamma and DRE2 sequences in the HP6 gene promoter in vitro.
###end p 124
###begin title 125
###xml 59 66 59 66 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">in vivo</italic>
DREF binds to the DRE2- and DRE1-containing genomic region in vivo

###begin p 126

###xml 960 1372 960 1372 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" textid="127">Binding of DREF to DRE-containing genomic regions of the <italic>HP6</italic> gene. ###xml 542 548 <span type="species:ncbi:9986">rabbit</span>
###xml 1113 1119 <span type="species:ncbi:9986">rabbit</span>
To further examine DREF-binding to the DRE1- and DRE2-containing region of the HP6 gene, primers to amplify the region from -66 to -167 and -856 to -1060 (Figure 2) were chemically synthesized and used for chromatin immunoprecipitation assays with anti-DREF polyclonal antibodies. It is well established that the Drosophila PCNA gene is regulated by the DREF pathway (1,11,12). Amplification of the PCNA gene promoter region containing the DRE in immunoprecipitates with the anti-DREF polyclonal antibody was 27-fold higher than with control rabbit IgG (Figure 4). In contrast, no amplification of the Actin 5C gene region was observed (Figure 4). Amplification of the HP6 gene promoter region containing the DRE1 in the immunoprecipitates with anti-DREF polyclonal antibody was 28-fold and that containing DRE2 was 13-fold (Figure 4). These results indicate that DREF binds to the genomic region containing DRE1 and DRE2 of the HP6 gene in S2 cells. Figure 4.Binding of DREF to DRE-containing genomic regions of the HP6 gene. Cross-linked chromatin of S2 cells was immunoprecipitated with anti-DREF IgG, control rabbit IgG or no IgG. The genomic regions containing DRE1 of the HP6 gene, DRE2 of the HP6 gene, DRE of the PCNA gene and Act5C gene were amplified by real time PCR and compared with the amplification products from the immunoprecipitates with the control IgG.
###end p 126

###xml 153 159 <span type="species:ncbi:9986">rabbit</span>

Effects of knockdown of the DREF gene on HP6 gene expression in cultured cells
###end title 128
###begin p 129
###xml 11 14 11 14 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HP6</italic>
###xml 110 113 110 113 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HP6</italic>

###xml 421 424 421 424 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HP6</italic>
###xml 497 505 497 505 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F5">Figure 5</xref>

###xml 686 695 683 692 <label xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Figure 5.</label>
###xml 843 847 840 844 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DREF</italic>

###xml 695 1057 692 1051 <p xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" textid="130">Effects of dsRNA treatment on mRNA levels of HP6 in S2 cells. cDNAs were prepared from total RNA isolated from dsRNA treated S2 cells and levels of <italic>DREF</italic>, <italic>HP6</italic> and <italic>&#946;-tubulin</italic> mRNAs were measured by quantitative RT-PCR. ###xml 695 1057 692 1051 <caption xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML"><p textid="130">Effects of dsRNA treatment on mRNA levels of HP6 in S2 cells. cDNAs were prepared from total RNA isolated from dsRNA treated S2 cells and levels of <italic>DREF</italic>, <italic>HP6</italic> and <italic>&#946;-tubulin</italic> mRNAs were measured by quantitative RT-PCR. ###xml 1057 1057 1051 1051 <graphic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xlink:href="gkn1068f5"/>
###xml 686 1057 683 1051 <fig xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" id="F5" position="float"><label>Figure 5.</label><caption><p textid="130">Effects of dsRNA treatment on mRNA levels of HP6 in S2 cells. cDNAs were prepared from total RNA isolated from dsRNA treated S2 cells and levels of <italic>DREF</italic>, <italic>HP6</italic> and <italic>&#946;-tubulin</italic> mRNAs were measured by quantitative RT-PCR. Fold differences against the amplification with no treatment (Mock) are shown with standard deviations from three independent dsRNA treatments.</p></caption><graphic xlink:href="gkn1068f5"/></fig>
Endogenous HP6 gene expression in RNAi-mediated DREF knockdown cells was examined to further demonstrate that HP6 is a DREF target gene. Total RNAs from double-stranded RNA (dsRNA)-treated S2 cells were isolated and quantitative RT-PCR was carried out (Figure 5). The DREF mRNA level was reduced by 82% in DREFdsRNA-treated cells, but not changed with LacZdsRNA-treatment. Under these conditions, the level of endogenous HP6 mRNA was decreased to 39%, while LacZdsRNA treatment exerted no effect (Figure 5). Expression of the beta-tubulin gene employed as a negative control was not affected by DREFdsRNA treatment. These results indicate that DREF is required for HP6 gene expression. Figure 5.Effects of dsRNA treatment on mRNA levels of HP6 in S2 cells. cDNAs were prepared from total RNA isolated from dsRNA treated S2 cells and levels of DREF, HP6 and beta-tubulin mRNAs were measured by quantitative RT-PCR. Fold differences against the amplification with no treatment (Mock) are shown with standard deviations from three independent dsRNA treatments.
###end p 129

###xml 1172 1178 <span type="species:ncbi:9986">rabbit</span>
We carried out RT-PCR to determine the HP6 expression pattern during Drosophila development (Figure 6). HP6 mRNA could be detected throughout all developmental stages but with the highest expression in adult males. Furthermore, the HP6 mRNA was expressed at least 6.3-fold higher in testes than in other parts of the body (Figure 6B). The observed HP6 expression pattern is consistent with the results reported by Greil et al. (37) and FlyAtlas (). Relatively high expression of both HP6 and DREF proteins in nuclei at the apical tips of testes was observed with immunostaining using anti-HP6 and anti-DREF antibodies (Figure 7B) and the specificity of anti-HP6 antibody binding was confirmed by western blot analysis with extracts from adult male flies expressing Flag-HP6 fusion protein (Figure 7A). The results suggest some specific role of HP6 during spermatogenesis. Figure 6.Developmental RT-PCR. ###begin title 135
DISCUSSION
###end title 135
###begin p 136
###xml 131 138 131 138 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T1">Table 1</xref>
###xml 143 151 143 151 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="fig" rid="F1">Figure 1</xref>
###xml 260 262 260 262 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B14">14</xref>
###xml 383 386 383 386 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HP6</italic>
###xml 388 394 388 394 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">pigeon</italic>
###xml 396 400 396 400 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lace</italic>
###xml 402 425 402 425 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">X box binding protein 1</italic>
###xml 427 432 427 432 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Xbp-1</italic>
###xml 438 445 438 445 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">guftagu</italic>
The present genetic screening of modifiers of the DREF-induced rough eye phenotype and identified 24 suppressors and 12 enhancers (Table 1 and Figure 1). Although these modifier genes are not necessarily transcriptional targets of DREF as reported previously (14), they could be critical genes in positive or negative regulation of the DREF pathway. By data base search, five genes, HP6, pigeon, lace, X box binding protein 1 (Xbp-1) and guftagu were found to carry DRE sequences in their 5'-flanking regions. These genes are therefore candidate DREF target genes. Nucleotide positions of DRE and DRE like sequences in the 5'-flanking regions of these genes are listed in the .
###end p 136
###begin p 137
###xml 4 7 4 7 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fat</italic>
###xml 86 88 86 88 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B39">39</xref>
###xml 89 91 89 91 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B40">40</xref>
###xml 124 133 124 133 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">armadillo</italic>
###xml 135 137 135 137 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B41">41</xref>
###xml 142 152 142 152 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 253 255 250 252 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B42">42</xref>
###xml 275 278 272 275 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fat</italic>
###xml 363 365 360 362 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B41">41</xref>
###xml 463 473 460 470 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 512 514 509 511 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B43">43</xref>
###xml 611 615 608 612 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">DREF</italic>
###xml 622 624 619 621 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B44">44</xref>
###xml 790 793 787 790 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">fat</italic>
###xml 846 850 843 847 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lace</italic>
###xml 883 887 880 884 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">lace</italic>
###xml 1064 1066 1061 1063 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B45">45</xref>
###xml 1194 1196 1191 1193 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B46">46</xref>
###xml 1302 1305 1299 1302 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">raf</italic>
###xml 1343 1353 1340 1350 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 1375 1377 1372 1374 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B21">21</xref>
###xml 1447 1451 1444 1448 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">star</italic>
###xml 1504 1511 1501 1508 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T1">Table 1</xref>
###xml 1671 1673 1668 1670 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B47">47</xref>
###xml 1743 1745 1740 1742 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B48">48</xref>
###xml 1786 1788 1783 1785 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B49">49</xref>
###xml 935 940 <span type="species:ncbi:4932">yeast</span>
The fat gene, one of the suppressors of the rough eye, encodes nonclassical cadherin (39,40) and genetically interacts with armadillo (41), a Drosophila homologue of mammalian beta-catenin and downstream effecter of the Wnt signal transduction pathway (42). Interaction with fat in the eye confirms the ability of this gene to modify cytoplasmic Armadillo level (41). When sufficient Armadillo protein accumulates in the cell, it forms a complex with Pangolin, a Drosophila homologue of mammalian T-cell factor (43). Previously we demonstrated that the Armadillo/Pangolin complex activates transcription of the DREF gene (44). We therefore suggest that suppression of the DREF-induced rough eye phenotype is caused by decrease of the Armadillo protein accumulation by half reduction of the fat gene dosage. The present screen also identified the lace gene as another suppressor. The lace gene encodes a membrane protein similar to the yeast protein LCB2, a subunit of serine palmitoyltransferase (SPT), which catalyses the first step of sphingolipid biosynthesis (45). It is now well known that sphingolipids trigger elevated levels of apoptosis via the modulation of known signaling pathways (46). Previously we reported that DREF is involved in regulation of vein formation through the activation of raf, downstream of Egfr signaling in the Drosophila wing imaginal discs (21). In accordance with this, the present genetic screen identified the star gene as one enhancer of the DREF-induced rough eye (Table 1). It encodes an integral membrane protein that is expressed in cells secreting Spitz and is localized in the early endoplasmic reticulum and nuclear envelope (47). Star interacts directly with Spitz, an activating ligand for Egfr (48), and regulates its protein expression (49).
###end p 137
###begin p 138
###xml 4 9 4 9 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Xbp-1</italic>
###xml 81 86 81 86 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Xbp-1</italic>
###xml 323 325 323 325 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B50">50</xref>
###xml 332 339 332 339 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">guftagu</italic>
###xml 385 395 385 395 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 425 427 425 427 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B51">51</xref>
###xml 595 597 595 597 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B51">51</xref>
###xml 636 651 636 651 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila skpA</italic>
###xml 678 680 678 680 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B52">52</xref>
###xml 687 691 687 691 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">skpA</italic>
###xml 984 986 980 982 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B53">53</xref>
###xml 1139 1141 1135 1137 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B45">45</xref>
###xml 1142 1144 1138 1140 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B46">46</xref>
###xml 1284 1289 1280 1285 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B54 B55 B56">54&#8211;56</xref>
###xml 1487 1489 1483 1485 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B57">57</xref>
The Xbp-1 gene is also a suppressor of the DREF-induced rough eye phenotype. The Xbp-1 gene encodes a 'bZIP'-containing transcription factor and plays a key role in the unfolded protein response, an evolutionarily conserved signalling pathway activated by an overload of misfolded proteins in the endoplasmic reticulum ER (50). The guftagu gene is an other suppressor that encodes the Drosophila Cullin-3 homologue (d-Cul3) (51) whose function impinges on the activity of many different signalling pathways and developmental events via targeted destruction or modification of specific proteins (51). Recently, we have reported that the Drosophila skpA gene is a target of DREF (52). The skpA gene encodes a component of the SCF complex that functions in combination with the ubiquitin conjugating enzyme UbcD1 and is involved in cell cycle regulation. Moreover regulation of the gene encoding the proteasome regulator REGgamma by the DRE/DREF system has also been reported by others (53). The ubiquitin-proteasome pathway plays key roles in many basic cellular processes, including immune responses, development and programmed cell death (45,46). In addition to degradation of defective or misfolded proteins, a critical regulatory role has been defined in studies of the cell cycle (54-56). Some major signal transduction pathways that are of great importance during development are known to be controlled in a coordinated way, in which the DRE/DREF pathway may be intimately involved (57).
###end p 138
###begin p 139
###xml 4 37 4 37 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eukaryotic initiation factor 3p40</italic>
###xml 39 46 39 46 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eIF3p40</italic>
###xml 53 60 53 60 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">dribble</italic>
###xml 69 90 69 90 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ribosomal protein S26</italic>
###xml 216 223 216 223 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="table" rid="T1">Table 1</xref>
###xml 292 294 292 294 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B58">58</xref>
###xml 300 304 300 304 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">krr1</italic>
###xml 391 393 391 393 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B59">59</xref>
###xml 702 704 702 704 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B60">60</xref>
###xml 705 707 705 707 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B61">61</xref>
###xml 714 735 714 735 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">ribosomal protein S26</italic>
###xml 751 761 751 761 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 814 816 814 816 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B62">62</xref>
###xml 1012 1014 1012 1014 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B63">63</xref>
###xml 1044 1049 1044 1049 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">eIF4A</italic>
###xml 1129 1131 1129 1131 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B64">64</xref>
###xml 1199 1200 1199 1200 <sup xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">7</sup>
###xml 1322 1324 1322 1324 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B65">65</xref>
###xml 1325 1327 1325 1327 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B66">66</xref>
###xml 802 805 <span type="species:ncbi:10116">rat</span>
The eukaryotic initiation factor 3p40 (eIF3p40), the dribble and the ribosomal protein S26 genes were included in the other suppressors identified in the screening and they are all associated with protein synthesis (Table 1). The dribble protein encodes a novel KRR1p-like KH domain protein (58) and krr1 mutations affect biogenesis of 18S rRNA and its precursors and 40S ribosomal subunits(59). The eIF3p40 protein encodes the p40 subunit of the eIF3 complex which facilitates charging of the 40S ribosomal subunit with the ternary complex (eIF2, Met-tRNAMet, GTP) and bridging with the eIF4G subunit of the cap-binding complex, eIF4F and inhibiting the association of 40S and 60S ribosomal subunits (60,61). The ribosomal protein S26 gene encodes a Drosophila ribosomal protein (RP) with homology to rat RP S26 (62). A slow growth rate and an altered adult size are thought to be the result of a reduced capacity for protein synthesis and this phenotype has been demonstrated to disrupt genes that encode RPs (63). Recently we identified the eIF4A gene, encoding a member of the DEAD box family of ATP-dependent RNA helicases (64), as another target of DREF. eIF4A is proposed to function in cap(m7GpppN)-dependent initiation of protein synthesis by unwinding the secondary structure of 5'-untranslated regions of mRNA (65,66). Since genes responsible for degradation of defective or misfolded proteins are targets of DREF as described above, DREF apparently promotes both protein synthesis and degradation by directly or indirectly activating genes involved in these processes. This is presumably associated with the active protein metabolism typical of proliferating cells.
###end p 139
###begin p 140
###xml 176 179 176 179 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HP6</italic>
###xml 231 234 231 234 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HP6</italic>
###xml 357 367 357 367 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 406 408 406 408 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B37">37</xref>
###xml 565 567 565 567 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B67">67</xref>
###xml 577 579 577 579 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B68">68</xref>
###xml 580 582 580 582 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B69">69</xref>
###xml 603 605 600 602 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B70">70</xref>
###xml 614 616 611 613 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B71">71</xref>
###xml 649 651 646 648 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B72">72</xref>
###xml 661 663 658 660 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B73">73</xref>
###xml 727 729 724 726 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B74">74</xref>
###xml 840 842 837 839 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B75">75</xref>
###xml 849 859 846 856 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">caravaggio</italic>
###xml 887 897 884 894 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">Drosophila</italic>
###xml 942 945 939 942 <italic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">HP6</italic>
###xml 1066 1067 1063 1064 <xref xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" ref-type="bibr" rid="B1">1</xref>
A number of other genes are of obvious interest given their physiological significance. Among the strongest suppressors of the DREF-induced rough eye phenotype was the mutated HP6 gene. The present studies clearly demonstrate that HP6 gene is one of the targets of DREF. Although HP6 is not a modifier of position effect variegation as are several of other Drosophila HPs, it carries chromo shadow domain (37). It has been shown that chromo shadow domain in HP1 is highly conserved across species and crucial for interaction with many proteins such as the SUV39H1 (67), SP100 (68,69), TIF1-beta(KAP-1) (70), Ku70 (71), lamin B receptor, HP1 itself (72), Ki-67 (73) and HP1/origin recognition complex-associated protein (HOAP) (74). It has further been reported that HP6 directly interacts with the Caravaggio protein in a two-hybrid assay (75). The caravaggio gene is otherwise known as Drosophila HOAP. We here found the expression level of HP6 mRNA to the highest in adult males and it much higher in testes than other sites. DREF is also expressed in the testis (1). The present study revealed that both proteins at least partially co-localize in nuclei at the apical tips of testes where cell proliferation actively occurs, suggesting some roles of HP6 in regulation of cell proliferation or transcription of the meiosis-related genes in testis.
###end p 140

rowspan="1" colspan="1"><italic>HP2</italic></td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">5&#8242;-aATCGATt</td><td rowspan="1" colspan="1">&#8722;489 to &#8722;495</td></tr><tr><td rowspan="1"
